## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()

- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix

+ fixed code
```

```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

60-assistanttext-
Perfect! I have completed the comprehensive bug analysis and written it to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here's a summary of the investigation:

## Summary

**Root Cause**: The Kubernetes scheduler's event-driven re-queueing system is missing support for ResourceSlice events, causing pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices to become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created.

**The Bug Chain**:
1. Pod arrives requesting DRA resources (no ResourceSlices exist yet)
2. `dynamicresources.Filter()` returns Unschedulable → pod moved to unschedulable queue
3. DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices
4. **BUG**: ResourceSlice events are silently dropped because:
   - ResourceSlice is NOT defined as a GVK constant in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
   - Cannot be registered in `dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()`
   - Not added to event handler registration map (`gvkMap`)
   - No event handlers are registered for ResourceSlice changes
   - Events are never delivered → pod never re-evaluated

**Proposed Fix**: 5 minimal code changes across 2 files:
1. Add ResourceSlice GVK constant to framework types
2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() 
3. Register ResourceSlice event handler in eventhandlers.go
4. Register ResourceSlice events in dynamicresources plugin
5. Implement QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice changes

The complete analysis with specific line numbers, code diffs, and detailed explanations has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all extenders scores for all nodes.\n791: \t\t// It is keyed with node name.\n792: \t\tallNodeExtendersScores := make(map[string]*framework.NodePluginScores, len(nodes))\n793: \t\tvar mu sync.Mutex\n794: \t\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n795: \t\tfor i := range extenders {\n796: \t\t\tif !extenders[i].IsInterested(pod) {\n797: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n798: \t\t\t}\n799: \t\t\twg.Add(1)\n800: \t\t\tgo func(extIndex int) {\n801: \t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Inc()\n802: \t\t\t\tdefer func() {\n803: \t\t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Dec()\n804: \t\t\t\t\twg.Done()\n805: \t\t\t\t}()\n806: \t\t\t\tprioritizedList, weight, err := which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\n65: type GVK string\n66: \n67: // Constants for GVKs.\n68: const (\n69: \t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\n70: \t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\n71: \t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\n72: \t//           - a Pod that is deleted\n73: \t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\n74: \t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\n75: \tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n76: \t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\n77: \t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n78: \t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n79: \t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n80: \t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n81: \t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuck in the\n82: \t// unschedulable pod pool.\n83: \t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n84: \t// See: \"PersistentVolumeClaim\"\n88: \tCSINode                 GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\"\n89: \tCSIDriver               GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\"\n90: \tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n97: \n98: \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n99: \t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \"*\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\n100: \t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\n101: \t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\n104: \t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\n105: \tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n106: )\n107: \n108: type ClusterEventWithHint struct {\n109: \tEvent ClusterEvent\n110: \t// QueueingHintFn is executed for the plugin rejected by this plugin when the above Event happens,\n111: \t// and filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n112: \t// It's an optional field. Pod gets moved from unschedulableQ to backoffQ or activeQ.\n121: // If it returns an error, we'll take the returned QueueingHint as `Queue` at the caller whatever we returned here so that\n122: // we can prevent the Pod from being stuck in the unschedulable pod pool.\n123: //\n124: // - `pod`: the Pod to be enqueued, which is rejected by this plugin in the past.\n125: // - `oldObj` `newObj`: the object involved in that event.\n126: //   - For example, the given event is \"Node deleted\", the `oldObj` will be that deleted Node.\n127: //   - `oldObj` is nil if the event is add event.\n128: // \tcase Queue:\n147: \t\treturn \"Queue\"\n148: \t}\n149: \treturn \"\"\n150: }\n151: \n152: // ClusterEvent abstracts how a system resource's state gets changed.\n153: // Resource represents the {
  "content": "# Bug Analysis: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` \u2014 Examined to identify GVK constants available in framework\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 Examined for EventsToRegister() implementation and Filter() method\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 Examined to understand how event handlers are registered based on GVK list\n- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` \u2014 Examined for unionedGVKs() function that builds event handler map\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` \u2014 Entry point to understand how scheduling failures trigger re-queueing\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 112 (`ScheduleOne()` method)\n   - When `schedulingCycle()` fails with `Unschedulable` status, `FailureHandler()` is called\n\n2. **FailureHandler calls**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 1068 (`handleSchedulingFailure()`)\n   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Queue re-evaluation triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 377 (`buildEvtResHandler()`)\n   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods\n\n4. **Events come from**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 395 (switch statement on `gvkMap`)\n   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`\n\n5. **gvkMap built by**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` line 525 (`unionedGVKs()` function)\n   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins\n\n6. **Events declared in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 381 (`EventsToRegister()`)\n   - Lists all events that should trigger pod re-evaluation when plugin rejects a pod\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 1139 (`nodeIsSuitable()`)\n   - Filter method fails when checking if a node has suitable resources (returns Unschedulable)\n   - This happens when no ResourceSlices exist yet\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Primary Issue (Line ~95 in types.go)**: ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant in the framework\n\n**Secondary Issue (Lines 381-412 in dynamicresources.go)**: ResourceSlice is not included in EventsToRegister()\n\n**Tertiary Issue (Lines 395-492 in eventhandlers.go)**: No case for framework.ResourceSlice in the event handler registration switch statement\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a **race condition in the event-driven queue re-evaluation system**:\n\n1. **The Problem**: When a pod requesting DRA devices arrives before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler marks the pod as Unschedulable because:\n   - The dynamicresources Filter plugin calls `nodeIsSuitable()`\n   - This function queries the ResourceSlices to determine if a node has suitable resources\n   - Since no ResourceSlices exist yet, the check fails and returns Unschedulable\n\n2. **Why the Pod Gets Stuck**: When ResourceSlices are created/updated after the pod is unschedulable:\n   - **ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant** in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Therefore, it cannot be used in the dynamicresources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method\n   - Without being registered, ResourceSlice events are never added to the `gvkMap`\n   - Without being in `gvkMap`, the scheduler's event handler registration code in `eventhandlers.go` never creates event handlers for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Without event handlers, ResourceSlice creation/update events are **silently dropped**\n   - The unschedulable pod is never moved to the activeQ for re-evaluation\n\n3. **Why This Happens**:\n   - The DynamicResourceAllocation (DRA) feature was added without completing the event handler integration\n   - ResourceSlice is a valid Kubernetes resource (resource.k8s.io/v1alpha2) but was never added to the framework's GVK constants\n   - The plugin's EventsToRegister() can only register events for GVKs defined in the framework\n\n### Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\nPod arrives (no ResourceSlices yet)\n    \u2193\nschedulingCycle() \u2192 SchedulePod()\n    \u2193\ndynamicresources.Filter() checks nodeIsSuitable()\n    \u2193\nnodeIsSuitable() queries ResourceSlices (finds none)\n    \u2193\nFilter returns Unschedulable \u2192 Pod added to unschedulablePodPool\n    \u2193\nDRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice\n    \u2193\nResourceSlice event occurs \u274c BUT...\n    \u274c No GVK defined for ResourceSlice in framework/types.go\n    \u274c Therefore, not in dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()\n    \u274c Therefore, not in gvkMap\n    \u274c Therefore, no event handler registered\n    \u274c Event is silently dropped\n    \u2193\nPod remains in unschedulablePodPool FOREVER \u274c\n```\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (after line 95)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (after line 492)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n \t\t\tif at&framework.Add != 0 {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Storage().V1().StorageClasses().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n```\n\n### 4. Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod requesting a resource may become schedulable when a ResourceSlice is created\n+\t\t// or updated with suitable resources for the node.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 5. Add QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice Changes\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 564 or at end of file before PostBind)\n\n```go\n// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange checks whether a ResourceSlice change makes an unschedulable pod schedulable.\n// A pod waiting for resource allocation may be schedulable once ResourceSlices are available with suitable resources.\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\t// Check if this pod uses dynamic resources\n\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, nil); err != nil {\n\t\t// Pod doesn't use any ResourceClaims or cannot be scheduled\n\t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// ResourceSlice changes might make this pod schedulable, so always queue it\n\t// (conservative approach since we can't easily determine which pod depends on which ResourceSlice)\n\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"ResourceSlice was added or updated, requeuing pod that uses dynamic resources\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why This Bug Occurs\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where:\n\n1. **Plugins declare events** via `EventsToRegister()` that should trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods\n2. **The scheduler collects these events** and builds a map of GVK \u2192 ActionType\n3. **Event handlers are registered** only for GVKs present in this map\n4. **When events occur**, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate pods\n\nThe DRA feature was added but **ResourceSlice was never added to the framework's GVK constants**. This means:\n- It cannot be declared in EventsToRegister()\n- It is never added to the event handler registration map\n- No handlers are registered for it\n- Events are silently dropped\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThis is a **silent failure** \u2014 no errors are logged, but pods get permanently stuck:\n- The scheduler correctly marks the pod as Unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist)\n- The pod should be re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available\n- But the re-evaluation never happens because the event is never delivered\n- The operator sees a pod stuck in Pending state indefinitely\n\n### Severity\n\n**Critical** \u2014 Pods requesting DRA resources will be permanently stuck if:\n1. A pod is created before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n2. This will work around the bug if pods are created after ResourceSlices exist\n3. But race conditions make this unpredictable in production\n\n### Fix Scope\n\nThe fix is minimal and consists of:\n1. Adding one GVK constant\n2. Adding one entry to the wildcard resource list\n3. Adding one case in the event handler switch statement\n4. Adding one event entry in the plugin's EventsToRegister()\n5. Adding one optional QueueingHintFn for efficiency\n\nThe fix is **backward compatible** and introduces no breaking changes.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

{
  "content": "# Bug Analysis: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` \u2014 Examined to identify GVK constants available in framework\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 Examined for EventsToRegister() implementation and Filter() method\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 Examined to understand how event handlers are registered based on GVK list\n- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` \u2014 Examined for unionedGVKs() function that builds event handler map\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` \u2014 Entry point to understand how scheduling failures trigger re-queueing\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 112 (`ScheduleOne()` method)\n   - When `schedulingCycle()` fails with `Unschedulable` status, `FailureHandler()` is called\n\n2. **FailureHandler calls**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` line 1068 (`handleSchedulingFailure()`)\n   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue\n\n3. **Queue re-evaluation triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 377 (`buildEvtResHandler()`)\n   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods\n\n4. **Events come from**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` line 395 (switch statement on `gvkMap`)\n   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`\n\n5. **gvkMap built by**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` line 525 (`unionedGVKs()` function)\n   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins\n\n6. **Events declared in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 381 (`EventsToRegister()`)\n   - Lists all events that should trigger pod re-evaluation when plugin rejects a pod\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` line 1139 (`nodeIsSuitable()`)\n   - Filter method fails when checking if a node has suitable resources (returns Unschedulable)\n   - This happens when no ResourceSlices exist yet\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` and `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Primary Issue (Line ~95 in types.go)**: ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant in the framework\n\n**Secondary Issue (Lines 381-412 in dynamicresources.go)**: ResourceSlice is not included in EventsToRegister()\n\n**Tertiary Issue (Lines 395-492 in eventhandlers.go)**: No case for framework.ResourceSlice in the event handler registration switch statement\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe bug is a **race condition in the event-driven queue re-evaluation system**:\n\n1. **The Problem**: When a pod requesting DRA devices arrives before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler marks the pod as Unschedulable because:\n   - The dynamicresources Filter plugin calls `nodeIsSuitable()`\n   - This function queries the ResourceSlices to determine if a node has suitable resources\n   - Since no ResourceSlices exist yet, the check fails and returns Unschedulable\n\n2. **Why the Pod Gets Stuck**: When ResourceSlices are created/updated after the pod is unschedulable:\n   - **ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant** in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n   - Therefore, it cannot be used in the dynamicresources plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method\n   - Without being registered, ResourceSlice events are never added to the `gvkMap`\n   - Without being in `gvkMap`, the scheduler's event handler registration code in `eventhandlers.go` never creates event handlers for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Without event handlers, ResourceSlice creation/update events are **silently dropped**\n   - The unschedulable pod is never moved to the activeQ for re-evaluation\n\n3. **Why This Happens**:\n   - The DynamicResourceAllocation (DRA) feature was added without completing the event handler integration\n   - ResourceSlice is a valid Kubernetes resource (resource.k8s.io/v1alpha2) but was never added to the framework's GVK constants\n   - The plugin's EventsToRegister() can only register events for GVKs defined in the framework\n\n### Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\nPod arrives (no ResourceSlices yet)\n    \u2193\nschedulingCycle() \u2192 SchedulePod()\n    \u2193\ndynamicresources.Filter() checks nodeIsSuitable()\n    \u2193\nnodeIsSuitable() queries ResourceSlices (finds none)\n    \u2193\nFilter returns Unschedulable \u2192 Pod added to unschedulablePodPool\n    \u2193\nDRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice\n    \u2193\nResourceSlice event occurs \u274c BUT...\n    \u274c No GVK defined for ResourceSlice in framework/types.go\n    \u274c Therefore, not in dynamicresources.EventsToRegister()\n    \u274c Therefore, not in gvkMap\n    \u274c Therefore, no event handler registered\n    \u274c Event is silently dropped\n    \u2193\nPod remains in unschedulablePodPool FOREVER \u274c\n```\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (after line 95)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (after line 492)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n \t\t\tif at&framework.Add != 0 {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Storage().V1().StorageClasses().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n```\n\n### 4. Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod requesting a resource may become schedulable when a ResourceSlice is created\n+\t\t// or updated with suitable resources for the node.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 5. Add QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice Changes\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 564 or at end of file before PostBind)\n\n```go\n// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange checks whether a ResourceSlice change makes an unschedulable pod schedulable.\n// A pod waiting for resource allocation may be schedulable once ResourceSlices are available with suitable resources.\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\t// Check if this pod uses dynamic resources\n\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, nil); err != nil {\n\t\t// Pod doesn't use any ResourceClaims or cannot be scheduled\n\t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// ResourceSlice changes might make this pod schedulable, so always queue it\n\t// (conservative approach since we can't easily determine which pod depends on which ResourceSlice)\n\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"ResourceSlice was added or updated, requeuing pod that uses dynamic resources\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why This Bug Occurs\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where:\n\n1. **Plugins declare events** via `EventsToRegister()` that should trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods\n2. **The scheduler collects these events** and builds a map of GVK \u2192 ActionType\n3. **Event handlers are registered** only for GVKs present in this map\n4. **When events occur**, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate pods\n\nThe DRA feature was added but **ResourceSlice was never added to the framework's GVK constants**. Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 177-193)\n\n```diff\n func UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n \treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n \t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n \t}\n }\n```\n\n### 3. Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (after line 492)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n \t\t\tif at&framework.Add != 0 {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Storage().V1().StorageClasses().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n```\n\n### 4. Add ResourceSlice Event Registration in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 410)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A pod requesting a resource may become schedulable when a ResourceSlice is created\n+\t\t// or updated with suitable resources for the node.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 5. Add QueueingHintFn for ResourceSlice Changes\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (after line 564 or at end of file before PostBind)\n\n```go\n// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange checks whether a ResourceSlice change makes an unschedulable pod schedulable.\n// A pod waiting for resource allocation may be schedulable once ResourceSlices are available with suitable resources.\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n\t// Check if this pod uses dynamic resources\n\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, nil); err != nil {\n\t\t// Pod doesn't use any ResourceClaims or cannot be scheduled\n\t\treturn framework.QueueSkip, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// ResourceSlice changes might make this pod schedulable, so always queue it\n\t// (conservative approach since we can't easily determine which pod depends on which ResourceSlice)\n\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"ResourceSlice was added or updated, requeuing pod that uses dynamic resources\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why This Bug Occurs\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where:\n\n1. **Plugins declare events** via `EventsToRegister()` that should trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods\n2. **The scheduler collects these events** and builds a map of GVK \u2192 ActionType\n3. **Event handlers are registered** only for GVKs present in this map\n4. **When events occur**, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate pods\n\nThe DRA feature was added but **ResourceSlice was never added to the framework's GVK constants**. This means:\n- It cannot be declared in EventsToRegister()\n- It is never added to the event handler registration map\n- No handlers are registered for it\n- Events are silently dropped\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThis is a **silent failure** \u2014 no errors are logged, but pods get permanently stuck:\n- The scheduler correctly marks the pod as Unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist)\n- The pod should be re-evaluated when ResourceSlices become available\n- But the re-evaluation never happens because the event is never delivered\n- The operator sees a pod stuck in Pending state indefinitely\n\n### Severity\n\n**Critical** \u2014 Pods requesting DRA resources will be permanently stuck if:\n1. A pod is created before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices\n2. This will work around the bug if pods are created after ResourceSlices exist\n3. But race conditions make this unpredictable in production\n\n### Fix Scope\n\nThe fix is minimal and consists of:\n1. Adding one GVK constant\n2. Adding one entry to the wildcard resource list\n3. Adding one case in the event handler switch statement\n4. Adding one event entry in the plugin's EventsToRegister()\n5. Adding one optional QueueingHintFn for efficiency\n\nThe fix is **backward compatible** and introduces no breaking changes.\n",

# Bug Analysis: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Files Examined

- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Examined to identify GVK constants available in framework
- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — Examined for EventsToRegister() implementation and Filter() method

- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — Examined for unionedGVKs() function that builds event handler map
- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point to understand how scheduling failures trigger re-queueing

   - This calls `AddUnschedulableIfNotPresent()` to move the pod to the unschedulable queue

   - When an event occurs, this calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to re-evaluate unschedulable pods

   - The switch statement registers event handlers only for GVKs present in `gvkMap`

   - Collects all GVK events declared in `EventsToRegister()` methods of plugins
